# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

Perfect! I've completed the task and created the `answer.json` file with comprehensive findings about HTTP connection manager route matching in Envoy.

## Summary

I've identified **23 C++ source files** that implement HTTP connection manager route matching in envoyproxy/envoy:

### Core Components:

1. **Route Matching & Virtual Host Selection** (source/common/router/):
   - `config_impl.cc/h` - Contains the `RouteMatcher` class which performs virtual host lookup via `findVirtualHost()` and route matching through `VirtualHostImpl` classes. Key classes include `PrefixRouteEntryImpl`, `PathRouteEntryImpl`, and `RouteEntryImplBase`.

2. **HTTP Connection Manager** (source/common/http/):
   - `conn_manager_impl.cc/h` - Manages route caching through `ActiveStream::route()` and handles route refresh when headers are modified
   - `conn_manager_utility.cc` - Connection manager utilities
   - `conn_manager_config.h` - Configuration interface

3. **Router Filter** (source/common/router/):
   - `router.cc/h` - Implements route action dispatch through the `Filter::decodeHeaders()` method

4. **Supporting Components**:
   - Configuration providers (rds_impl.cc, vhds.cc)
   - Scoped routing (scoped_config_impl.cc)
   - Header parsing and metadata matching
   - Filter configuration (extensions/filters/network/http_connection_manager/ and extensions/filters/http/router/)

The implementation follows a three-stage process:
1. **Virtual host selection** based on authority/host header
2. **Route matching** using path, method, headers, and other criteria
3. **Route action dispatch** to determine cluster, redirect, or direct response

All findings have been saved to `/workspace/answer.json`.

            "content": "189:    streams. Each stream handles a single request and response.\n190: 6. For each HTTP stream, an :ref:`Downstream HTTP filter <arch_overview_http_filters>` chain is created and\n191:    runs. The request first passes through CustomFilter which may read and modify the request. The\n192:    most important HTTP filter is the router filter which sits at the end of the HTTP filter chain.\n193:    When ``decodeHeaders`` is invoked on the router filter, the route is selected and a cluster is\n194:    picked. The request headers on the stream are forwarded to an upstream endpoint in that cluster.\n195:    The :ref:`router <arch_overview_http_routing>` filter obtains an HTTP :ref:`connection pool\n196:    <arch_overview_conn_pool>` from the cluster manager for the matched cluster to do this.\n197: 7. Cluster specific :ref:`load balancing <arch_overview_load_balancing>` is performed to find an\n198: ",

            "startLine": 189

          {
            "content": "441: \n442: When ``decodeHeaders()`` is invoked on the :ref:`router <arch_overview_http_routing>` filter, the\n443: route selection is finalized and a cluster is picked. The HCM selects a route from its\n444: ``RouteConfiguration`` at the start of HTTP filter chain execution. This is referred to as the\n445: *cached route*. Filters may modify headers and cause a new route to be selected, by asking HCM to\n446: clear the route cache and requesting HCM to reevaluate the route selection.
